‚óŹ User approved Claude's plan
  ‚éŅ ¬†Plan saved to: ~/.claude/plans/load-the-wip-docs-typed-waffle.md ¬∑ /plan to
     edit
     Slice 1 of system+permissions: the eff permission (uniform, 
     pure-by-default, enforced, propagating)

     Context

     Model locked (docs/wip/feature-plan/system-and-permissions.md): two kinds
     map/system; signature
     <kind> <selector> (<writes>) [eff]; writes explicit, branch derived, eff an
     explicit
     permission. We do this properly ‚ÄĒ full model, no staging hack ‚ÄĒ sliced for
     tractability, each slice fully
     correct on its own:

     - Slice 1 (this plan): the eff permission ‚ÄĒ uniform on both kinds,
     pure-by-default, enforced as a
     hard error, propagating up. each is removed; its meaning becomes map + eff.
     - Slice 2: explicit (writes) signature replacing body-inferred read/write.
     - Slice 3: collapse HirMapDecl/HirEachDecl/HirSystemDecl into one decl +
     permission flags.
     - Slice 4: placement/residency derivation reads the signature.

     After slice 1: a map/system without eff is pure (running any effect is a
     hard error); map + eff
     is the effectful per-entity fan (the old each); system + eff is the effect
     composer. branch/E0046 are
     unchanged here (pure map stays branchless; eff lifts E0046 to allow the
     each-style body).

     Approach

     1. Effect detection ‚ÄĒ a kernel-appropriate walk (semantic/semantic.c)

     purity_walk() (4812) already finds effects but counts ordinary
     column/global writes as impure (correct for
     funcs, wrong for kernels ‚ÄĒ a kernel exists to write its columns). Add
     kernel_effect_walk() (a sibling /
     a mode flag on purity_walk) that flags true side-effects ‚ÄĒ
     insert/delete/dealloc
     (name_is_archetype_mutating_builtin 4678), extern/#foreign/@syscall/proc
     calls
     (func_call_effect_reason), running an Eff (TYK_EFF run, 4831), I/O ‚ÄĒ but
     not writes to the kernel's
     own selected columns. It keeps purity_walk's recursion, so effects inside a
     nested each/map fan are
     found ‚Üí propagation falls out for free.

     2. Parse + carry eff (parser/parser.c, hir/hir.h, lower/lower.c)

     - Parser: after the selector ) of map/system/each and before {, accept an
     optional bare eff
     keyword (cur_ident_is("eff",3)); record it on the decl node. (Map parse
     ~1537, system ~1571, each ~1602.)
     - HIR: add int eff to the kernel decls.
     - map (Q) eff lowers to the each path (HirEachDecl via lower_each_payload
     ~2477) so it reuses the
     per-entity effectful-fan codegen unchanged; a plain map stays HirMapDecl.

     3. Enforce + flip the default (semantic/semantic.c, sem_diagnostics.c)

     - New hard diagnostic effect_without_eff (next free E02xx).
     - In analyze_system_decl (6658), analyze_each_decl (6680), and inline-each
     (6714): run
     kernel_effect_walk(body); if it reports an effect and the decl lacks eff ‚Üí
     emit the error
     (reason + location). This flips system/each to pure-by-default. map is
     already pure (E0046); eff
     on a map lifts E0046 (routes to the each body).
     - Propagation is automatic: a pure system containing an effectful nested
     map/each ‚Üí the walk finds the
     nested effect ‚Üí error "runs effects via a nested kernel; declare eff".

     4. Migration ‚ÄĒ automated codemod (~628 kernels)

     ~611 effectful systems + 17 each decls must gain eff / become map + eff.
     Build a codemod: with
     enforcement on, the compiler errors at each effectful-but-no-eff kernel; a
     script iterates the errors and
     inserts  eff before that decl's { (and rewrites each (Q) { ‚Üí map (Q) eff 
     {). Run across
     tests/, stdlib/, examples/, extras/, self-hosted/; re-run until the suite
     is green. (Per
     [[known-failures-and-committed-tests]]: this edits committed tests via a
     reviewed codemod, never deletes;
     inspect the diff before committing.)

     5. Design doc

     Update docs/wip/feature-plan/system-and-permissions.md: mark the three
     decisions resolved, record the
     slice order, and state the each ‚Üí map + eff removal.

     Critical files

     - semantic/semantic.c ‚ÄĒ kernel_effect_walk (model on purity_walk¬†4812); the
     eff-required check in
     analyze_{system,each}_decl + inline-each; lift E0046 when map.eff.
     - semantic/sem_diagnostics.c ‚ÄĒ register effect_without_eff.
     - parser/parser.c ‚ÄĒ optional trailing eff on map/system/each headers.
     - hir/hir.h, lower/lower.c ‚ÄĒ eff field; map+eff ‚Üí each payload.
     - A migration script (scratch) + the ~628 edited .arche files.

     Verification

     - New tests: (a) system { insert(...) } with no eff ‚Üí effect_without_eff
     error; (b) system eff { insert(...) } ‚Üí ok;
     (c) pure system { col = expr } (no eff) ‚Üí ok and unchanged; (d) map (Q) eff
     { effect + control flow }
     ‚Č° the old each (same output); (e) propagation: pure system { map (Q) eff { 
     effect } } ‚Üí error.
     - Pure map/system codegen unchanged; map+eff runs as each; effectful system
     eff runs as today.
     - Full lit -q tests/ extras/ green after the codemod; make test-gpu-exe
     green; rebuild clean.
     - Spot-check the codemod diff on a few files (correct kernels gained eff;
     pure ones didn't).

     Honest scale note

     This is a large but mechanical migration (~628 kernels) ‚ÄĒ the cost of an
     honest pure-by-default flip done in
     one coherent landing rather than a deprecation window. The codemod +
     full-suite gate is what makes it safe.

‚óŹ Slice 1 is complete and fully green. Here's the summary.

  Slice 1 landed: the eff permission

  The locked model ‚ÄĒ <kind> <selector> (<writes>) [eff], writes explicit, branch
  derived ‚ÄĒ is now real for its first slice: system is pure by default, and
  running effects requires the eff permission.

  Compiler changes
  - Parser (parser.c, syntax_tree.h/.c): eff is a contextual keyword after a
  map/system/each selector, parsed to an SN_EFF marker. The formatter
  round-trips it (verify-fmt green).
  - HIR/lower (hir.h, lower.c): decls carry int eff; map (Q) eff lowers to the
  each payload ‚ÄĒ it is the old each, reusing that codegen unchanged.
  - Semantic (semantic.c, sem_diagnostics.*): new kernel_effect_body_view (=
  purity_walk in kernel_mode ‚ÄĒ column/singleton reads+writes are data work, not
  effects; insert/delete, extern/proc calls, running an Eff, and a bare
  Eff-typed statement are). A system running an effect without eff ‚Üí new hard
  error E0226 effect_without_eff. The walk recurses into nested kernels, so
  propagation is automatic. map (Q) eff lifts the pure-map E0046 restriction;
  pure map keeps it.

  Migration (~628 kernels)
  - A codemod inserted eff after the selector of every flagged effectful system
  ‚ÄĒ 622 .arche files. core/stdlib needed nothing (they're funcs/procs, no
  systems).
  - Hand-fixed the non-codemod sites: doctest wrapper, arche init templates, C
  test fixtures, extras/gfx device systems, a few device/cli fixtures, and
  effectful examples in README/language.md/patterns.md.

  Verification ‚ÄĒ all green
  - lit tests/ extras/: 888/888 (incl. 5 new tests/unit/language/permissions/
  regression tests covering effect-required, eff-ok, pure-ok, map+eff ‚Č° each,
  and propagation)
  - check-corpus, test-gpu-exe, verify-fmt (927 files), and all C unit suites
  (semantic/codegen/lower/hotreload/inspect/syntax-view)

  Two honest caveats
  1. each kept as sugar, not removed. It's now semantically map + eff (lowers
  identically), but the keyword stays because inline map (Q) eff as a statement
  has no lowering yet (the compiler aborts on it ‚ÄĒ pre-existing, confirmed with
  plain inline map too). Keyword removal is deferred until inline-map statements
  are supported. I updated the design doc to state this rather than ship a
  half-working removal.
  2. make test-doc is red on docs/language.md + docs/patterns.md ‚ÄĒ but I stashed
  my changes and rebuilt master to confirm: those two fail identically on
  master (discarded_ok lint, unknown archetype Pending), with zero eff-related
  errors. Pre-existing doc rot, not my regression; left alone.

  Nothing is committed (per your workflow). The design doc
  (docs/wip/feature-plan/system-and-permissions.md) now records the slice order,
  the three resolved decisions, and the each status.

‚óŹ Update(docs/patterns.md)
  ‚éŅ ¬†Added 1 line, removed 1 line
      106  "route the row into the pool for that case," and an absent row
            is simply never read ‚ÄĒ no per-step guards,
      107  no intra-row effect‚Üíeffect chaining. **Consuming = deleting**:
            a handled row leaves the pool, so it is
      108  never re-processed on a later pass (a drained pool re-runs to 
           nothing). This is the shape of arche-rpg's
      109 -`done :: each (Closed)`: it fires only once a `Closed` row exi
          -sts, so "should we exit?" needs no boolean ‚ÄĒ                  
      109 +`done :: map (Closed) eff`: it fires only once a `Closed` row 
          +exists, so "should we exit?" needs no boolean ‚ÄĒ               
      110  the row's presence is the signal.

      375  A `system` takes **no parameters and returns nothing**. It is 
           named in a `#run` schedule and the
      376  runtime runs it; a program's **entry point is a `#run` schedul
           e**, not a decl named `main` (a `main`
      377  decl is a hard error, [E0225](explain/E0225.md)). To run an ef
           fect **per matching row**, use
      378 -`each (query { ‚Ä¶ })` ‚ÄĒ the effectful sibling of `map`: where a
          - `map` body is a branch-free column                           
      379 -kernel, an `each` body may branch, call, `insert`/`delete`, an
          -d run effects, once per row. Being a                          
      380 -sequential per-element fan, it is a loop: `continue` skips the
          - rest of the current element and advances to                  
      381 -the next row (guard-clause style). There is no `break` ‚ÄĒ stopp
          -ing a fan early is incoherent.                                
      378 +`map (query { ‚Ä¶ }) eff` ‚ÄĒ the effectful per-entity fan: where 
          +a plain `map` body is a branch-free column                    
      379 +kernel, a `map ‚Ä¶ eff` body may branch, call, `insert`/`delete`
          +, and run effects, once per row (this is                      
      380 +what the removed `each` keyword spelled). Being a sequential p
          +er-element fan, it is a loop: `continue`                      
      381 +skips the rest of the current element and advances to the next
          + row (guard-clause style). There is no                        
      382 +`break` ‚ÄĒ stopping a fan early is incoherent.                 
      383  
      384  `proc` is **reserved for the foreign boundary** ‚ÄĒ only a `#for
           eign`/`@syscall`/`@intrinsic`
      385  declaration (or a `@drop` hook) is a `proc`. A non-foreign `pr
           oc` is an error

      435  A map body is **only** column transforms (`col = expr`). It is
            a loopless, branch-free kernel:
      436  the runtime owns the iteration, so the same source vectorizes

       1  # Systems and permissions ‚ÄĒ the unified kernel model
       2  
       3 -> **Status: in progress ‚ÄĒ Slice 1 (`eff`) landed.** The model u
         -nifies the three kinds (`map` / `each` /                       
       4 -> `system`) to **`map` + `system`** with `each` as **`map + eff
         -`**, under an **explicit permission                            
       5 -> signature** `<kind> <selector> (<writes>) [eff]`. Slice 1 ‚ÄĒ t
         -he **`eff` permission** ‚ÄĒ is implemented;                      
       6 -> the remaining slices (explicit `(writes)`, decl collapse, pla
         -cement derivation) are below.                                  
       3 +> **Status: in progress ‚ÄĒ Slice 1 (`eff`) landed; `each` keywor
         +d removed.** The model unifies the kinds                       
       4 +> to **`map` + `system`** under an **explicit permission signat
         +ure** `<kind> <selector> (<writes>) [eff]`.                    
       5 +> The effectful per-entity fan is now spelled **`map (Q) eff`**
         + (the `each` keyword is gone ‚ÄĒ `each` is an                    
       6 +> ordinary identifier). Slice 1 ‚ÄĒ the **`eff` permission** ‚ÄĒ is

‚óŹ Update(docs/explain/W0030.md)
  ‚éŅ ¬†Added 4 lines, removed 3 lines
      10  - **`func`** ‚ÄĒ pure value code. It produces results either as a
           single `-> T` return **or** as an
      11    out-parameter list `func(in)(out, ‚Ä¶)` (the form `proc` used t
          o carry, for multiple results or filling a
      12    caller buffer). A func performs no effects.
      13 -- **`system` / `each`** ‚ÄĒ the effect leaves and composer. A `sy
         -stem` runs effects (an `Eff` with `()`,                        
      14 -  a `#foreign` proc, `insert`/`delete`, `fmt.printf`) over ambi
         -ent pool state; an `each (query{‚Ä¶})` is the                    
      15 -  per-row effectful fan. They take no value parameters ‚ÄĒ they r
         -ead the world's columns in place.                              
      13 +- **`system` / `map (Q) eff`** ‚ÄĒ the effect leaves and composer
         +. A `system` runs effects (an `Eff` with                       
      14 +  `()`, a `#foreign` proc, `insert`/`delete`, `fmt.printf`) ove
         +r ambient pool state; a `map (query{‚Ä¶}) eff`                   
      15 +  is the per-row effectful fan (with the `eff` permission). The
         +y take no value parameters ‚ÄĒ they read the                     
      16 +  world's columns in place.                                    
      17  - **`map`** ‚ÄĒ the pure, branch-free data-parallel kernel.
      18  
      19  The program's entry is a **`#run`** schedule, not a `main`.

      301  // PROPOSED ‚ÄĒ state as data, one branchless step per tick. Sta
           tes linear so "phase complete" = +1:
      302  //   NEED_HDR = 0, NEED_BODY = 1, DONE = 2.   `want - have` is

      303  //   (want = HDR in phase 0, want = HDR + len in phase 1), so

           ed, else 0   (mask)

            once DONE   (mask)
      307    recv(fd, req)(buf, got:);  have = have + got;

‚óŹ each is removed. 890/890 green.

  What changed

  The keyword is gone ‚ÄĒ the effectful per-entity fan is now map (Q) eff 
  everywhere:
  - Parser: map (Q) eff switches the node kind to SN_EACH_EXPR, so it reuses all
  the existing fan machinery (HirEachDecl, analyze_each_decl, the codegen
  row-loop) ‚ÄĒ top-level and inline statement position (inline map (Q) eff no
  longer segfaults). The as w row-binder parses inside the parens (map (Q as w) 
  eff); as without eff is a hard error.
  - Reverted the now-dead Slice-1 map+eff routing in
  lower_map_from/analyze_map_decl (map nodes never carry eff anymore ‚ÄĒ it's
  encoded by the node kind).
  - TOK_EACH removed from the lexer, parser, and token-category ‚ÄĒ each is now an
  ordinary identifier. The SN_EACH_EXPR node and its machinery stay (they're
  what map (Q) eff lowers to).

  Migration (codemod each_codemod.py, line-based, handles /// doc code, skips //
  and #each_field):
  - All each (...) sites rewritten to map (...) eff ‚ÄĒ including stdlib (router,
  plus http's multi-line each hand-fixed), tests, extras, examples, self-hosted,
  design_analysis.
  - Two new regression tests: each_keyword_removed.arche (keyword stays gone)
  and map_eff_as_requires_eff.arche.

  Docs updated: README, docs/language.md, docs/patterns.md (gated ‚ÄĒ fences +
  prose + tables + TOC), docs/explain/W0030.md, the wip/ docs, and my
  feature-plan doc (which I'd left saying the opposite ‚ÄĒ now corrected: each
  removed, inline + as supported).

  Verification ‚ÄĒ all green

  - lit tests/ extras/: 890/890
  - check-corpus, test-gpu-exe, verify-fmt (927), all C unit suites
  (semantic/codegen/lower/hotreload/inspect/syntax-view)
  - test-doc: unchanged ‚ÄĒ only the pre-existing Pending/discarded_ok rot in
  docs/language.md+docs/patterns.md (verified on master), no each/eff
  regressions.

  pervasive concept and you curate that folder ([[user-curated-docs]]). Their
  code fences now reference the removed keyword. Want me to sweep those too, or

  ‚éŅ ¬†Plan saved to: ~/.claude/plans/load-the-wip-docs-typed-waffle.md ¬∑ /plan to
     edit
     Slice 2 of system+permissions: the explicit (writes) signature

     Context

     The unified-kernel model (docs/wip/feature-plan/system-and-permissions.md)
     locks the kernel signature as
     <kind> <selector> (<writes>) [eff], write-set explicit. Slice 1 (the eff
     permission,
     pure-by-default) and the each-keyword removal are landed and green. This
     slice makes the write-set a
     declared, checked part of the header for selector-bound columns.

     Pivotal finding from exploration: the compiler has no read/write inference 
     today. lower_query_columns
     (lower/lower.c:2411) and HirParam.is_own (hir/hir.h:126) track only the own
     ownership keyword, not
     which columns a body writes; SN_ASSIGN_STMT handling (semantic.c:~3187)
     type-checks but never collects a
     per-kernel write-set. The "derive read/write from how a kernel touches a
     pool" in
     docs/wip/migration-derived-placement.md is design-only (confirmed: no
     placement/branchless analysis
     exists; only @gpu/@resident decorators + an eff flag).

     So this slice does two things: (a) add the explicit (writes) declaration,
     and (b) build the body
     write-analysis that checks it ‚ÄĒ kernel_write_walk, the sibling of Slice 1's
     kernel_effect_walk. That
     walk is the load-bearing new capability: it makes (writes) a checked
     contract, powers the automated
     migration, and is exactly the per-column write fact the future placer
     (Slice 4) reads off the signature.

     Scope (user decisions):
     - Slice 2 only. Slice 3 (HIR decl collapse) and Slice 4 (placement +
     showcase bench) are out of scope.
     - (writes) covers selector-bound columns only (bare names from a
     query/archetype selector).
     - Whole-column direct init R.v = { ‚Ä¶ } in a run-once system stays legal and
     is not part of
     (writes) (it's bulk init, not a selector-bound per-element write).
     - Indexed pool writes inside a selector kernel (R.v[i] = ‚Ä¶ within a map /
     query-system / fan) become
     a hard error ‚ÄĒ the bound bare column must be used. Outside a selector
     (run-once systems, loaders like
     csv.load filling Transaction.price[idx]), indexed writes stay the existing
     W0029 lint. (Because
     W0029 fires "outside a query," inside-selector indexed writes are already
     rare ‚áí this sub-migration is
     expected to be near-zero; verify during impl.)

     Surface

     arche
     step    :: map (Movers) (pos, vel) { pos += vel; vel -= ‚Ä¶ }      //
     declares writes pos, vel
     clampit :: map (query { v }) (v) eff { if (v > 2.5) { v = 2.5; } } //
     (writes) then eff
     shade   :: map (query { pos, color }) (color) { color = pack(pos); } //
     reads pos, writes color
     peek    :: map (query { v }) { x := v + 1; }                     // no
     (writes) ‚áí writes nothing
     seed    :: system { R.v = { 0.0, 1.0, ‚Ä¶ }; fmt.printf(‚Ä¶); }      //
     run-once bulk init: legal, no (writes)
     // inside a selector kernel, `R.v[i] = ‚Ä¶` is now an ERROR ‚ÄĒ use the bound
     bare column `v`.

     (writes) sits after the selector ), before the optional eff: a comma list
     of bound columns the
     body assigns. Writing a bound column not listed is a hard error; a selector
     kernel that writes but omits
     (writes) errors and names the inferred set (drives the codemod).

     Approach

     1. Parse (writes) (parser/parser.c, syntax/syntax_tree.{h,c})

     Add parse_opt_writes() mirroring parse_opt_eff/parse_opt_row_bind
     (parser.c:1462-1488) and the
     out-param list parse parse_proc_out_list (parser.c:588). Match an optional
     ( right after the selector
     ), parse a comma list of bare column names each wrapped SN_WRITE_PARAM,
     close ). Slot into the map
     and system branches of parse_primary_expr (parser.c:1569-1645) after 
     match(RPAREN), before
     parse_opt_eff ‚ÄĒ for map: parse_opt_writes(); if (parse_opt_eff()) *out_kind
     = SN_EACH_EXPR; (writes
     survive the map‚Üíeach routing). Add SN_WRITE_PARAM to the SyntaxNodeKind
     enum + the name table.

     2. Carry it (hir/hir.h, lower/lower.c, semantic DeclSummary)

     Add char **writes; int write_count; to HirMapDecl/HirSystemDecl/HirEachDecl
     (hir.h:155-192); fill in
     lower_{map,system,each}_* (lower.c:2467-2514) via sv_count/sv_child_at(f, 
     SN_WRITE_PARAM, ‚Ä¶). Mirror on
     the semantic DeclSummary so the checker can read the declaration.

     3. Build kernel_write_walk (semantic/semantic.c)

     New walk (sibling of purity_walk/kernel_effect_walk) over a kernel body
     collecting bound-column
     assignment targets: for each SN_ASSIGN_STMT/compound-assign, resolve the
     LHS base; if it is a bound
     selector column (incl. tuple-group pos.x ‚Üí pos) record it (bare); recurse
     into nested inline fans. Two
     products: the actual write-set (for the (writes) check) and detection of an
     indexed pool write inside a
     selector (LHS is Pool.col[idx] while a selector/current_map_archetype is in
     scope) ‚Üí the new error.

     4. Check + enforce (semantic/semantic.c, sem_diagnostics.{h,c})

     In analyze_map_decl/analyze_system_decl/analyze_each_decl
     (semantic.c:6684-6792): run
     kernel_write_walk, compare to declared (writes). New diagnostics (next free
     E02xx):
     - write_set_missing ‚ÄĒ selector kernel writes bound column(s) but has no
     (writes) (names the set;
     the codemod reads it).
     - write_undeclared ‚ÄĒ writes a bound column not in (writes).
     - write_unused (warning) ‚ÄĒ a declared column the body never writes.
     - indexed_write_in_selector ‚ÄĒ indexed pool write R.v[i]=‚Ä¶ inside a selector
     kernel. (Reuse the
     W0029 detection point at semantic.c:5925: when the indexed pool access is
     an assignment LHS and a
     selector is in scope, emit this hard error instead of the W0029 lint.)

     5. Migrate ‚ÄĒ automated codemod (scratch, like Slice 1)

     With the checker on, the compiler errors at each selector kernel
     missing/mismatching (writes), naming the
     columns. A codemod inserts  (col, ‚Ä¶) after the selector ) (before any eff),
     iterating to green across
     tests/, stdlib/, examples/, extras/, self-hosted/, design_analysis/ (reuse
     the selector-scan
     from the Slice-1 codemod). Separately migrate any inside-selector indexed
     writes the new error flags
     (expected ~none) to the bound bare column. Inspect the diff; never delete
     ([[known-failures-and-committed-tests]]).

     6. Tests + docs

     New tests/unit/language/permissions/ tests: declared==actual ok; undeclared
     write ‚Üí error; missing
     (writes) ‚Üí error; over-declared ‚Üí warning; (writes)+eff ordering; run-once
     system bulk init needs
     no (writes); indexed write inside a selector ‚Üí error; indexed write in a
     loader (no selector) ‚Üí still
     allowed (W0029). Update system-and-permissions.md (mark (writes) resolved)
     and the docs/language.md/
     README signature descriptions.

     Critical files

     - parser/parser.c ‚ÄĒ parse_opt_writes; slot into map/system branches.
     - syntax/syntax_tree.h + .c ‚ÄĒ SN_WRITE_PARAM kind + name.
     - hir/hir.h, lower/lower.c ‚ÄĒ writes/write_count on the three kernel decls;
     fill lower_*_from.
     - semantic/semantic.c ‚ÄĒ kernel_write_walk; the check + indexed-write error
     in analyze_{map,system,each};
     branch the W0029 site (5925) to a hard error for inside-selector indexed
     writes.
     - semantic/sem_diagnostics.{h,c} ‚ÄĒ
     write_set_missing/write_undeclared/write_unused/
     indexed_write_in_selector.
     - migration codemod (scratch) + migrated .arche files.

     Verification

     - New permission tests pass.
     - Full lit tests/ extras/ green after the codemod; check-corpus, make 
     test-gpu-exe, verify-fmt, and
     the C unit suites
     (test-semantic/test-codegen-unit/test-lower/test-hotreload/test-inspect/
     test-syntax-view) green. make test-doc unchanged (pre-existing
     Pending/discarded_ok rot only).
     - Generated code unchanged ‚ÄĒ declaration/typing change, not codegen
     (spot-check IR for one kernel
     before/after). csv.load and the bounds-proving !abort tests still compile
     (loaders unaffected).

     Honest scale note

     The correctness work is small; the (writes) migration is large (most
     selector kernels write a bound
     column, so most gain a (writes) list) ‚ÄĒ automated like Slice 1's via
     kernel_write_walk + error-driven
     codemod + the full-suite gate. The indexed-write ban is scoped to
     inside-selector writes only, so it spares
     loaders and is expected to touch ~0 existing sites. The walk is reused by
     Slice 4, so the cost buys the
     placement foundation, not just a syntax tax.

      1492 + * between the selector `)` and the optional `eff`. Returns 1
           + if a list was parsed. */                                    
      1493 +static int parse_opt_writes(Parser *parser) {                
      1494 +  if (!check(parser, TOK_LPAREN))                            
      1495 +    return 0;                                                
      1496 +  advance(parser); /* consume '(' */                         
      1497 +  if (!check(parser, TOK_RPAREN)) {                          
      1498 +    do {                                                     
      1499 +      if (!check(parser, TOK_IDENT)) {                       
      1500 +        error(parser, "Expected a column name in the `(writes
           +)` list ‚ÄĒ `map (Movers) (pos, vel) { ‚Ä¶ }`");                 
      1501 +        return 0;                                            
      1502 +      }                                                      
      1503 +      int w_cp = syntax_cp(parser);                          
      1504 +      advance(parser); /* the column name */                 
      1505 +      syntax_wrap(parser, w_cp, SN_WRITE_PARAM);             
      1506 +    } while (match(parser, TOK_COMMA) && !check(parser, TOK_R
           +PAREN));                                                     
      1507 +  }                                                          
      1508 +  if (!match(parser, TOK_RPAREN)) {                          
      1509 +    error(parser, "Expected ')' to close the `(writes)` list"
           +);                                                           
      1510 +    return 0;                                                
      1511 +  }                                                          
      1512 +  return 1;                                                  
      1513 +}                                                            
      1514 +                                                             
      1515  /* `out_kind` receives the SyntaxNodeKind for the primary exp
            ression form parsed,
      1516   * derived from parse context (not from a built AST node). Th
            e caller wraps the
      1517   * syntax tree node with it. Left untouched when the primary 
            already wrapped itself (paren). */

      6708  
      6709 +/* ===== Slice 2: the `(writes)` permission ===== */         
      6710 +                                                             
      6711 +/* Record a bound-column write (deduped) into the active per-
           +kernel collector. */                                         
      6712 +static void kernel_record_write(SemanticContext *ctx, const c
           +har *col) {                                                  
      6713 +  if (!col)                                                  
      6714 +    return;                                                  
      6715 +  for (int i = 0; i < ctx->k_write_count; i++)               
      6716 +    if (strcmp(ctx->k_writes[i], col) == 0)                  
      6717 +      return; /* dedup */                                    
      6718 +  ctx->k_writes = realloc(ctx->k_writes, (size_t)(ctx->k_writ
           +e_count + 1) * sizeof(char *));                              
      6719 +  ctx->k_writes[ctx->k_write_count++] = sem_dupz(col);       
      6720 +}                                                            
      6721 +                                                             
      6722 +/* Begin collecting bound-column writes for a kernel body. Sa
           +ves the parent collector (so a nested inline                 
      6723 + * fan's writes don't leak to its enclosing system) and start
           +s fresh. */                                                  
      6724 +static void kernel_writes_begin(SemanticContext *ctx, int *sv
           +_collect, char ***sv_w, int *sv_n) {                         
      6725 +  *sv_collect = ctx->k_collect;                              
      6726 +  *sv_w = ctx->k_writes;                                     
      6727 +  *sv_n = ctx->k_write_count;                                
      6728 +  ctx->k_collect = 1;                                        
      6729 +  ctx->k_writes = NULL;                                      
      6730 +  ctx->k_write_count = 0;                                    
      6731 +}                                                            
      6732 +                                                             
      6733 +/* Check the collected actual write-set against the kernel's 
           +declared `(writes)` (SN_WRITE_PARAM children of              
      6734 + * `knode`); emit E0227 if any actual bound-column write is u
           +ndeclared (or the list is absent). Over-declaring            
      6735 + * is permitted (forward-compatible; avoids false positives o
           +n any write form the collector misses). Then free            
      6736 + * this kernel's collector and restore the parent's. */      
      6737 +static void kernel_writes_end(SemanticContext *ctx, SyntaxVie
           +w knode, const char *kind, const char *name,                 
      6738 +                              SourceLoc loc, int sv_collect, 
           +char **sv_w, int sv_n) {                                     
      6739 +  int nd = sv_count(knode, SN_WRITE_PARAM);                  
      6740 +  int missing = 0;                                           
      6741 +  for (int i = 0; i < ctx->k_write_count && !missing; i++) { 
      6742 +    int found = 0;                                           
      6743 +    for (int j = 0; j < nd && !found; j++) {                 
      6744 +      const char *dn = sv_token(sv_child_at(knode, SN_WRITE_P
           +ARAM, j), TOK_IDENT);                                        
      6745 +      if (dn && strcmp(dn, ctx->k_writes[i]) == 0)           
      6746 +        found = 1;                                           
      6747 +    }                                                        
      6748 +    if (!found)                                              
      6749 +      missing = 1;                                           
      6750 +  }                                                          
      6751 +  if (missing) {                                             
      6752 +    size_t cap = 4;                                          
      6753 +    for (int i = 0; i < ctx->k_write_count; i++)             
      6754 +      cap += strlen(ctx->k_writes[i]) + 2;                   
      6755 +    char *list = malloc(cap);                                
      6756 +    size_t p = 0;                                            
      6757 +    list[p++] = '(';                                         
      6758 +    for (int i = 0; i < ctx->k_write_count; i++) {           
      6759 +      if (i) {                                               
      6760 +        list[p++] = ',';                                     
      6761 +        list[p++] = ' ';                                     
      6762 +      }                                                      
      6763 +      size_t l = strlen(ctx->k_writes[i]);                   
      6764 +      memcpy(list + p, ctx->k_writes[i], l);                 
      6765 +      p += l;                                                
      6766 +    }                                                        
      6767 +    list[p++] = ')';                                         
      6768 +    list[p] = '\0';                                          
      6769 +    sem_emit_write_set_mismatch(ctx, loc, kind, name, list, n
           +d > 0);                                                      
      6770 +    free(list);                                              
      6771 +  }                                                          
      6772 +  for (int i = 0; i < ctx->k_write_count; i++)               
      6773 +    free(ctx->k_writes[i]);                                  
      6774 +  free(ctx->k_writes);                                       
      6775 +  ctx->k_collect = sv_collect;                               
      6776 +  ctx->k_writes = sv_w;                                      
      6777 +  ctx->k_write_count = sv_n;                                 
      6778 +}

‚óŹ Three clear issues. The most important: E0228 is too broad ‚ÄĒ it fires on
  foreign pool indexed writes (Config.gravity[0] in a map), preempting W0024. It
  should only fire for the kernel's own selector pool (where a bound column
  exists); foreign pools have no bound name and stay W0024's domain. Let me
  refine it.

‚óŹ Slice 2 is complete and fully green.

  Slice 2 landed: the explicit (writes) signature

  The kernel signature is now <kind> <selector> (<writes>) [eff] ‚ÄĒ a selector
  kernel declares the bound columns it assigns, and the compiler checks it.

  The key realization (from exploration): there was no read/write inference to
  "replace" ‚ÄĒ so this slice built the body write-analysis, the way Slice 1 built
  kernel_effect_walk. That walk is the per-column write fact Slice 4's placer
  will read straight off the signature.

  Implementation
  - Parse (parser.c, syntax_tree.{h,c}): parse_opt_writes ‚Üí SN_WRITE_PARAM
  children, slotted after the selector ) and before eff in both map/system
  branches.
  - Carry (hir.h, lower.c): writes/write_count on the three kernel decls.
  - Enforce (semantic.c): writes are collected during the analyze pass (columns
  in scope as is_param), accumulated per-kernel with save/restore across nested
  fans, then compared to the declaration.
    - E0227 write_set_mismatch ‚ÄĒ writes an undeclared/omitted bound column
  (message names the full set, which drives the codemod). Over-declaring is
  allowed (keeps the check sound).
    - E0228 indexed_write_in_selector ‚ÄĒ R.v[i] = ‚Ä¶ inside a selector for the
  kernel's own pool. Foreign pools stay W0024; loaders/run-once stay the W0029
  lint, so csv.load and seeding keep working.

  Migration (writes_codemod.py, E0227-driven): 91 .arche files + hand-fixes to
  the arche init template, a C test fixture, the formatter test's RUN-line, and
  the README/language.md doc fences.

  One bug worth noting: the SemanticContext is malloc'd (not calloc'd), so the
  new accumulator fields were garbage and segfaulted until explicitly
  initialized ‚ÄĒ caught and fixed.

  tests), check-corpus, test-gpu-exe, verify-fmt (934), all C unit suites.

‚óŹ User approved Claude's plan
  ‚éŅ ¬†Plan saved to: ~/.claude/plans/load-the-wip-docs-typed-waffle.md ¬∑ /plan to
     edit
     Slice 3 of system+permissions: collapse the three kernel decls into one

     Context

     The model (docs/wip/feature-plan/system-and-permissions.md) is two kinds ‚ÄĒ 
     map + system ‚ÄĒ plus
     permission flags (eff, (writes), branch-derived). Slices 1 (eff) and 2
     ((writes)) landed and are
     committed; each is gone from the surface. But the HIR still carries the old
     three-way split:
     HirMapDecl / HirEachDecl / HirSystemDecl, with tags HIR_DECL_MAP /
     HIR_DECL_EACH /
     HIR_DECL_SYSTEM. These three structs are now nearly identical (all carry
     name/params/stmts/eff/writes/loc;
     map adds is_gpu, each adds row_var), and the "each" tag is just map + eff.
     This slice collapses them
     into one HirKernelDecl + a kind field + permission flags, so the IR matches
     the locked model and
     Slice 4's placer can read a kernel's permissions (kind / eff / writes /
     is_gpu) uniformly off one struct
     instead of branching across three union members.

     Pure internal refactor ‚ÄĒ no behavior change, no .arche migration. The C
     compiler flags every stale
     data.map/data.each/data.system, so the build won't link until every site is
     converted; the full test
     suite (already exercising all three paths) is the correctness gate. (User
     chose the full collapse: one
     struct + one tag + kind, not a struct-only unify that keeps the three
     tags.)

     Target shape (hir/hir.h)

     typedef enum { HIR_KERNEL_MAP, HIR_KERNEL_SYSTEM } HirKernelKind;
     typedef struct {
         char *name;
         HirKernelKind kind;   /* MAP = individual; SYSTEM = column / run-once 
     composer */
         HirParam **params; int param_count;
         HirStmt **stmts;   int stmt_count;
         int eff;              /* may run effects; MAP+eff is the per-entity fan
     (the old `each`) */
         int is_gpu;          /* @gpu ‚ÄĒ pure map only (kind==MAP && !eff) */
         char **writes; int write_count;
         char *row_var;       /* MAP+eff `as w` row handle, else NULL */
         SourceLoc loc;
     } HirKernelDecl;

     - HirDeclKind: remove HIR_DECL_MAP/HIR_DECL_EACH/HIR_DECL_SYSTEM, add
     HIR_DECL_KERNEL.
     - HirDecl.data union: replace map/each/system members with one
     HirKernelDecl *kernel.
     - HIR_STMT_EACH's payload (data.each_stmt) becomes HirKernelDecl * (inline
     fan = MAP+eff).

     The mapping every consumer uses:
     - old pure map ‚Üí kind==MAP, eff==0
     - old each / map (Q) eff ‚Üí kind==MAP, eff==1
     - old system ‚Üí kind==SYSTEM

     Approach

     1. HIR (hir/hir.h, hir/hir.c)

     Define HirKernelDecl + HirKernelKind; swap the enum tags + union member. In
     hir.c: replace the three
     hir_{map,system,each}_decl_free with one hir_kernel_decl_free and the three
     free-switch arms with one
     case HIR_DECL_KERNEL. Fix the pre-existing leaks while here (the old frees
     skipped params/writes/
     writes[i]/row_var) ‚ÄĒ free them all in the unified free.

     2. Producers (lower/lower.c)

     - lower_map_from ‚Üí HIR_DECL_KERNEL, kernel->kind=MAP, eff=0.
     - lower_each_payload ‚Üí returns HirKernelDecl* with kind=MAP, eff=1 (used by
     both lower_each_from
     and the inline HIR_STMT_EACH site ~line¬†1148).
     - lower_system_from ‚Üí kind=SYSTEM.
     - The alternate SN_MAP_DECL map path (~line¬†2800) ‚Üí kind=MAP (retype;
     behavior preserved).
     - is_gpu set site in lower_decl_cst (~2930): gate on kernel->kind==MAP.
     - expand_group_assigns retyped to HirKernelDecl*.

     3. Codegen dispatch (codegen/codegen.c) ‚ÄĒ the bulk

     Keep the three emit functions (codegen_map_decl / codegen_each_decl /
     codegen_system_decl), retyped to
     take HirKernelDecl*; change only the dispatch keys to kind+eff:
     - Decl emit loop (~13128): case HIR_DECL_KERNEL: ‚Üí kind==SYSTEM ‚Üí system;
     else eff ‚Üí each(fan);
     else ‚Üí map.
     - emit_sched (~11950): kind==SYSTEM ‚Üí call void; kind==MAP && eff ‚Üí call 
     void (fan);
     kind==MAP && !eff ‚Üí HIR_STMT_RUN carrying is_gpu.
     - cg_find_scheduled_decl (~11930): just d->data.kernel->name (no per-kind
     branch).
     - find_map_decl (~1375): match kind==MAP && !eff (the pure scheduled map).
     - HIR_STMT_RUN handler (~9769) + GPU gate (~9878): unchanged logic; keep
     gpu gated on the pure map
     (is_gpu, only set there).
     - HIR_STMT_EACH handler (~10014): data.each_stmt now HirKernelDecl* ‚Üí
     codegen_each_fan reads
     params/stmts/row_var as before.
     - emit_cross_unit_declares (~12873): kind==MAP && !eff ‚Üí map trampoline
     (matching archs); else
     (fan or system) ‚Üí bare-name trampoline.
     - Helpers map_query_cols / collect_map_matching_archs /
     collect_map_foreign_pools retyped to
     HirKernelDecl* (logic unchanged).

     4. GPU + tests glue

     - codegen/gpu_glsl.c: gpu_glsl_mark_runs + arche_gpu_emit branch on
     kind==HIR_DECL_KERNEL &&
     kernel->kind==MAP. codegen/gpu_glsl.h: HirMapDecl* ‚Üí HirKernelDecl* in the
     two signatures.
     - tests/unit/compiler/lower_tests.c (~278): the kind != HIR_DECL_MAP filter
     ‚Üí kind != HIR_DECL_KERNEL.

     Critical files

     hir/hir.h, hir/hir.c, lower/lower.c, codegen/codegen.c (bulk),
     codegen/gpu_glsl.c,
     codegen/gpu_glsl.h, tests/unit/compiler/lower_tests.c. No .arche files
     change.

     Verification

     Pure refactor ‚áí the existing suite is the oracle (no new tests):
     - Clean rebuild links (every stale data.map/each/system is a compile error
     ‚ÄĒ that's the coverage that
     nothing was missed).
     - lit tests/ extras/ 897/897; check-corpus, make test-gpu-exe, verify-fmt,
     and the C unit suites
     (test-semantic/test-codegen-unit/test-lower/test-hotreload/test-inspect/tes
     t-syntax-view) green;
     make test-doc unchanged (pre-existing Pending/discarded_ok only).
     - Spot-check emitted IR is byte-identical before/after for one
     representative of each path (a pure map,
     a map (Q) eff fan, a system) ‚ÄĒ confirms no behavior drift.
     - The permissions tests (tests/unit/language/permissions/) and
     tests/unit/language/each/ exercise all
     three lowering‚Üícodegen paths; they must stay green.

     Notes / non-goals

     - No surface syntax change; eff/(writes)/@gpu behave exactly as today.
     - Slice 4 (placement derivation + the derived-placement showcase benchmark)
     stays out of scope; this slice
     is the IR cleanup that makes the placer read permissions off one struct.

‚óŹ Slice 3 is complete and verified clean.

  Slice 3 landed: the three kernel decls collapsed into one

  The HIR now matches the locked two-kinds model. The three near-identical
  structs HirMapDecl / HirEachDecl / HirSystemDecl (and tags
  HIR_DECL_MAP/EACH/SYSTEM) are gone, replaced by:

  - One HirKernelDecl with a kind field (HIR_KERNEL_MAP | HIR_KERNEL_SYSTEM) +
  the permission flags (eff, is_gpu, writes, row_var), under one tag
  HIR_DECL_KERNEL / data.kernel.
  - The mapping every consumer uses: pure map = MAP && !eff; the per-entity fan
  (old each / map (Q) eff) = MAP && eff; system = SYSTEM.

  Scope of the change:
  - hir.h/hir.c: unified struct/enum/union; one hir_kernel_decl_free that also 
  fixes pre-existing leaks (the old frees skipped
  params/writes/writes[i]/row_var).
  - lower.c: all producers emit HIR_DECL_KERNEL; the several identical switches
  collapsed; the two MAP-only asymmetries (param-type rename in hir_rn,

‚ĚĮ before we do this. The reason its runtime is because every pc it runs on has  
  different cost metrics, no? which means there needs to be a seperate step     
  inbetween runtime and compiletime. Like a per user comptime or something, no? 

‚óŹ You're exactly right, and it's the sharpest framing of the whole problem. Let
  me make the case precise, because it actually resolves the tension rather than
  just relocating it.

  Why placement is runtime in prior art ‚ÄĒ and the gap you spotted

  StarPU/Legion decide per-task at runtime for two reasons: (1) dynamic data 
  sizes and (2) machine-specific cost constants ‚ÄĒ GPU launch latency, PCIe
  up/down bandwidth, CPU vs GPU throughput. A cost model baked at author compile
  time is blind to (2): the same .ll ships to a 4090 and a laptop iGPU, and a
  single hardcoded threshold is wrong on almost every box. That's the hole in a
  naive "static arithmetic-intensity cost model" ‚ÄĒ which is exactly the option I
  had teed up, and you correctly rejected it.

  The resolution: a per-machine phase, then freeze the decision

  Your "per-user comptime" is the right shape ‚ÄĒ a third phase between 
  author-compile and run:

  1. Author compile (machine-independent): emit IR + the derived facts ‚ÄĒ
  eligibility (kind==MAP && !eff), access sets, arithmetic intensity per kernel.
  2. Per-machine calibration/specialization (once, at install / first run on
  this box): microbenchmark the machine ‚Üí a profile of cost constants (launch
  overhead, PCIe BW, CPU & GPU throughput). Feed profile + derived facts into
  the placement decision, and freeze it into the binary (or a sidecar plan).
  3. Runtime: just executes the frozen plan. No runtime scheduler, no per-task 
  cost evaluation ‚ÄĒ arche's core bet is preserved.

  The key arche-specific reason this works where it wouldn't for StarPU: static 
  pools. Because there's no dynamic allocation, problem sizes are known at 
  compile time too. So at the per-machine phase you have every cost input ‚ÄĒ
  machine constants (calibrated) + arithmetic intensity (derived) + row counts
  (static pool capacity). Nothing is left for runtime to discover. That's
  precisely what lets the mapper fold into a per-machine compile step instead of
  a runtime scheduler.

  This is well-precedented (so it's sound, not speculative)

  - FFTW "wisdom" ‚ÄĒ measures the machine, produces a plan, reuses it. The
  canonical calibrate-once-then-freeze.
  - ATLAS ‚ÄĒ install-time empirical autotuning per machine.
  - StarPU's own perfmodels ‚ÄĒ per-machine history/regression calibration in
  ~/.starpu‚Ä¶ but consulted at runtime. arche's move is to consult it once and
  freeze.
  - TVM/Ansor, Halide autoschedulers ‚ÄĒ measure the target, then specialize.
  - -march=native / Gentoo / Android ART AOT-on-install ‚ÄĒ the
  per-machine-compile family.

  The mechanism isn't novel; the combination is the point (consistent with the
  earlier kill-pass): static pools + derived access facts + calibrated constants
  ‚Üí a fully frozen, no-runtime-scheduler placement. It also corrects
  static-mapper.md, which currently says "fold the mapper into the compiler" ‚ÄĒ
  it should say "fold it into a per-machine calibration phase."

  What this means for Slice 4

  The cost model must read a machine profile, not hardcoded constants ‚ÄĒ so Slice
  4 grows a calibration step. That's bigger, and naturally splits. Let me get
  your intent on how much to build now.

‚óŹ¬†User declined to answer questions
  ‚éŅ ¬†¬∑ Folding in the per-machine calibration phase: how much of it should Slice
     4 build now? (Profile format + cost model, stub calibration / Full 
     calibration harness too / Design doc first, then build)

‚ĚĮ so then arche run can fold it together and arche build can ... work exactly   
  how? hmmm                                                                     

‚óŹ Right ‚ÄĒ let's trace it, because the command model basically falls out, and
  it's cleaner than it first looks.

  The thing that collapses it: arche build is already per-machine

  arche compiles from source on the host ‚ÄĒ like gcc, not like shipping a .jar.
  So arche build already runs on your box. That means for the common case (you
  build and run on the same machine), the "separate per-user phase" you're
  reaching for isn't separate ‚ÄĒ it's just more work inside arche build, exactly
  the way gcc -march=native specializes to the build host. The per-machine step
  you intuited is real; it just lives inside build when build-host == target.

  So:

  - arche build (default, target = this machine): consult a cached machine 
  profile; if it's missing, run calibration once and cache it (FFTW-wisdom style
  ‚ÄĒ ~/.fftw, StarPU's ~/.starpu, or arche's existing ARCHE_CACHE_DIR from the
  incremental work). Then: derive facts (eligibility, access sets, intensity) +
  static pool sizes + profile ‚Üí decide placement ‚Üí freeze it into the binary. No
  runtime scheduler.
  - arche run = build + execute. So "run folds it together" = yes, trivially ‚ÄĒ
  it's build (which now includes the per-machine placement) then run the frozen
  plan.
  - Calibration is a cached side-input, measured once per machine, not paid
  every build.

  That's the whole local story, and it needs no new command ‚ÄĒ just a profile
  cache + a cost model that reads it, added to the build.

  The only case that needs a genuine separate phase: shipping elsewhere

  Build on A, run on B (distribution) is the one place the host ‚Č† target, so A's
  arche build can't know B's costs. Three known shapes, all opt-in behind
  something like --portable / --target=generic:

  1. Calibrate-on-target: ship the binary + a calibrator; first run on B
  measures B and writes a frozen plan sidecar. (Closest to your "per-user
  comptime" as a literal install step.)
  2. Fat binary: emit both CPU and GPU variants per eligible kernel + a one-time
  first-run selector that picks per-machine and freezes the choice.
  3. Ship IR: B's arche finishes placement (true per-machine AOT, like Android
  ART on-install).

  All three keep the "no runtime scheduler" property ‚ÄĒ the decision is made once
  on B and frozen, never per-task.

  So arche build works exactly how

  ‚Ėé Default: specialize to this machine. Read-or-create the cached machine 
  ‚Ėé profile ‚Üí fold placement in ‚Üí native binary. A --portable flag defers 
  ‚Ėé placement to a first-run/install step on the target.

  Which means the honest scoping question is really which world Slice 4 targets 
  first ‚ÄĒ and local-dev (build == run host) is both the common case and the one
  that needs zero new infrastructure beyond a cached profile + cost model.
  Distribution is a clean follow-on once the local mechanism exists.

  Does that match how you're picturing it ‚ÄĒ local-first, build folds in the
  per-machine placement, distribution later? Or are you thinking the calibration
  should be its own visible command (arche calibrate) even in the local case?

‚úĽ Saut√©ed for 11m 40s

‚óŹ Locked: local-first, placement folds into arche build (per-machine, cached
  profile), distribution later. That's the architecture. Let me write the Slice
  4 plan around it.

     edit
     Slice 4 of system+permissions: derived placement via a per-machine 
     calibration phase (local-first)

     Context

     Slices 1‚Äď3 made the kernel signature explicit and uniform (HirKernelDecl:
     kind + eff + writes + is_gpu),
     so the placer can read a kernel's permissions off one struct. This slice
     derives CPU/GPU placement from
     that signature instead of the @gpu annotation ‚ÄĒ and resolves the
     long-standing tension head-on.

     The realization (this session): placement is a runtime decision in prior
     art (StarPU/Legion) for two
     reasons ‚ÄĒ dynamic data sizes and machine-specific cost constants (GPU
     launch overhead, PCIe bandwidth,
     CPU vs GPU throughput). A cost model hardcoded at author-compile time is
     blind to the second and is wrong on
     almost every box. The fix is a per-machine calibration phase whose decision
     is frozen (no runtime
     scheduler ‚ÄĒ arche's core bet survives). Two things make it tractable here:

     1. Static pools ‚áí row counts are known at compile time, so the calibration
     phase has every cost input:
     calibrated machine constants + derived arithmetic intensity + static
     problem size. Nothing is left for
     runtime to discover (unlike StarPU, where sizes are dynamic).
     2. arche compiles from source on the host (like gcc -march=native). So for
     the common case
     (build-host == run-host) the per-machine phase folds into arche build ‚ÄĒ no
     new command. A machine
     profile is measured once and cached (FFTW-wisdom / ~/.starpu style, in
     ARCHE_CACHE_DIR), reused
     across builds. arche run = build (now placement-aware) + execute.

     Post-Slice-3, GPU-eligibility is free: branchless ‚ąß effect-free = kind==MAP
     && !eff (a pure map). The
     open cell is profitability ‚ÄĒ which eligible maps actually go GPU ‚ÄĒ and this
     slice gives it a concrete,
     machine-calibrated v1.

     Prior art for the calibrate-once-then-freeze phase: FFTW wisdom, ATLAS, 
     StarPU perfmodels (we freeze
     instead of consulting at runtime), TVM/Ansor, -march=native/ART-on-install.
     Mechanism well-precedented;
     the combination (static pools + derived facts + calibrated constants ‚Üí
     fully frozen, no-runtime-scheduler
     placement) is the point.

     Scope (locked with user): local-first (build-host == target). Derive
     placement (CPU vs GPU) only;
     residency stays annotated (@resident/gpu.sync) ‚ÄĒ its derivation (needs a
     read-walk) is Slice 5.
     Distribution (--portable, build ‚Č† run host) is a follow-on. Honest caveat:
     on this box (GTX 1650 /
     PCIe) GPU loses to CPU on launch+transfer overhead for all but deliberately
     compute-heavy kernels ‚ÄĒ so
     the deliverable is correct, calibrated decisions + a real profile, and the
     bench needs a compute-heavy arm
     to actually show a GPU win (otherwise it honestly shows CPU winning).

     Approach

     1. Derived facts (author-compile, machine-independent)

     - Eligibility = kind==MAP && !eff over the existing gate (1 matching float
     pool, ‚Č§64 cols,
     codegen.c:~9879). Free.
     - Arithmetic intensity: a small body walk over a pure map counting
     arithmetic ops (flops) and the
     column-byte traffic it touches (params √ó elem_size). Per-element; multiply
     by static row count at the
     decision. Reuse the statement/expr-walk infra (e.g. mirror
     kernel_write_walk shape in semantic.c).

     2. Machine profile + cache (cli/, a new small module)

     - A MachineProfile struct of cost constants: gpu_present, gpu_launch_us,
     pcie_up_gbps,
     pcie_down_gbps, cpu_gflops, gpu_gflops (extend later). Serialized to
     ARCHE_CACHE_DIR/machine.profile.
     - arche build reads it; if absent/stale, runs calibration once and caches
     it. arche calibrate forces a
     re-measure (thin wrapper; optional).

     3. Calibration (minimal, reuse runtime/gpu_runtime.c)

     - cpu_gflops: time a known float kernel. gpu_launch_us: time a tiny/empty
     arche_gpu_dispatch.
     pcie_*_gbps: time a sized host‚ÜĒdevice transfer. gpu_gflops: time a known
     GPU kernel. No Vulkan/device
     ‚áí gpu_present=0 ‚áí CPU-only placement (honest fallback; matches no---gpu
     today).

     4. Placement decision (in build, frozen ‚ÄĒ the hook)

     - At codegen.c:~11965 (rs.data.run_stmt.is_gpu = ‚Ä¶ kernel->is_gpu), replace
     with:
     eligible(map) && cost_model(profile, intensity, rows) predicts GPU faster ‚áí
     dispatch GPU. The decision is
     baked into the emitted @arche_run schedule (the existing is_gpu run-flag) ‚ÄĒ
     static, no runtime eval.
     - Cost model: GPU_t = launch_us + bytes/pcie_bw + flops/gpu_gflops (+ 
     download); CPU_t = flops/cpu_gflops; pick the min. Transparent,
     profile-driven.
     - @gpu stays as a force-GPU override (skips the cost model) ‚ÄĒ keeps the
     bench's A/B and lets a user pin
     placement; un-annotated pure maps are now placed by derivation.

     5. Showcase benchmark (no annotations)

     - One program, two arms over identical static pools, neither annotated: a
     memory-bound map (‚Čą1 op/
     element ‚Üí model picks CPU) and a compute-heavy map (many ops/element, e.g.
     iterated transcendentals ‚Üí
     model may pick GPU). Report, per arm: the derived decision (CPU/GPU), the
     cost-model estimate, and measured
     wall time. Honest about whether GPU actually wins on this hardware.

     6. Docs

     - Amend static-mapper.md: "fold the mapper into the compiler" ‚Üí "fold it
     into a per-machine arche build
     calibration phase" (three-phase model: derived facts ‚Üí calibrated profile ‚Üí
     frozen decision).
     - Amend migration-derived-placement.md ¬ß5‚Äď¬ß6: placement = build-time,
     per-machine, cached profile;
     static pools supply the sizes; distribution (--portable) later.

     Critical files

     - semantic.c (or a new placement.c): arithmetic-intensity walk; the cost
     model + decision.
     - new machine-profile module + calibration (reuse runtime/gpu_runtime.c
     dispatch/timing).
     - codegen/codegen.c:~11965 (decision hook) + ~9879 (eligibility gate).
     - cli/cmd_build.c (calibrate-if-absent; --portable stub note); optional
     cli/cmd_calibrate.c.
     - design_analysis/benchmarks/‚Ä¶ (the showcase) + the two design docs.

     Verification

     - New tests: a pure map with no @gpu builds + runs correctly under the
     derived decision (CPU on this
     box); the cost-model decision for a compute-heavy vs memory-bound map
     matches expectation; the profile
     cache is created then reused (second build skips calibration); @gpu
     force-override still dispatches
     GPU; no-Vulkan ‚áí CPU-only, clean.
     - Full lit tests/ extras/, check-corpus, make test-gpu-exe, verify-fmt, all
     C unit suites green;
     test-doc unchanged.
     - Bench builds + runs, prints the derived decisions, estimates, and
     measured times (honest result).

     Honest scope notes / non-goals

     - Profitability is a v1 calibrated heuristic, not "solved"; the
     contribution is the per-machine-static
     architecture + correct, reproducible decisions ‚ÄĒ not a guaranteed GPU win
     on this hardware.
     - Out of scope (follow-ons): residency derivation (read-walk ‚Üí replace
     @resident/gpu.sync, Slice¬†5);
     distribution (--portable: calibrate-on-target / fat binary / ship-IR);
     richer cost models (divergence,
     occupancy).

‚óŹ Update(codegen/codegen.c)
  ‚éŅ ¬†Added 63 lines
      1373    return prog ? prog : "reject";
      1374  }
      1375  
      1376 +/* ===== Derived placement: arithmetic-intensity estimate + c
           +ost model (Slice 4) ===== */                                 
      1377 +                                                             
      1378 +/* Coarse per-element arithmetic-op count of an expression (b
           +inary/unary ops; a call is weighted, callees                 
      1379 + * not inlined ‚ÄĒ a v1 estimate). A pure map body is straight-
           +line/branchless, so this captures its compute                
      1380 + * density. */                                               
      1381 +static double cg_expr_flops(const HirExpr *e) {              
      1382 +  if (!e)                                                    
      1383 +    return 0;                                                
      1384 +  switch (e->kind) {                                         
      1385 +  case HIR_EXPR_BINARY:                                      
      1386 +    return 1.0 + cg_expr_flops(e->data.binary.left) + cg_expr
           +_flops(e->data.binary.right);                                
      1387 +  case HIR_EXPR_UNARY:                                       
      1388 +    return 1.0 + cg_expr_flops(e->data.unary.operand);       
      1389 +  case HIR_EXPR_CALL: {                                      
      1390 +    double f = 8.0; /* math builtin / func call ‚ÄĒ a coarse we
           +ight (transcendentals are pricey) */                         
      1391 +    for (int i = 0; i < e->data.call.arg_count; i++)         
      1392 +      f += cg_expr_flops(e->data.call.args[i]);              
      1393 +    return f;                                                
      1394 +  }                                                          
      1395 +  case HIR_EXPR_FIELD:                                       
      1396 +    return cg_expr_flops(e->data.field.base);                
      1397 +  case HIR_EXPR_INDEX: {                                     
      1398 +    double f = cg_expr_flops(e->data.index.base);            
      1399 +    for (int i = 0; i < e->data.index.index_count; i++)      
      1400 +      f += cg_expr_flops(e->data.index.indices[i]);          
      1401 +    return f;                                                
      1402 +  }                                                          
      1403 +  default:                                                   
      1404 +    return 0;                                                
      1405 +  }                                                          
      1406 +}                                                            
      1407 +                                                             
      1408 +/* Per-element flop estimate of a kernel body (assignment / b
           +ind RHSs). */                                                
      1409 +static double cg_kernel_flops_per_elem(const HirKernelDecl *k
           +) {                                                          
      1410 +  double f = 0;                                              
      1411 +  for (int i = 0; i < k->stmt_count; i++) {                  
      1412 +    const HirStmt *s = k->stmts[i];                          
      1413 +    if (!s)                                                  
      1414 +      continue;                                              
      1415 +    if (s->kind == HIR_STMT_ASSIGN)                          
      1416 +      f += cg_expr_flops(s->data.assign_stmt.value);         
      1417 +    else if (s->kind == HIR_STMT_BIND)                       
      1418 +      f += cg_expr_flops(s->data.bind_stmt.value);           
      1419 +  }                                                          
      1420 +  return f;                                                  
      1421 +}                                                            
      1422 +                                                             
      1423 +/* The cost model: predict whether running this eligible map 
           +on the GPU beats the CPU, given the per-machine              
      1424 + * profile, the body's per-element flop count, the float-colu
           +mn count (4 bytes each), and the static row                  
      1425 + * count. GPU pays a fixed launch + the PCIe round-trip; CPU 
           +pays only compute. Static pools give `rows` at               
      1426 + * build time, so this is a fully build-time decision (frozen
           + ‚ÄĒ no runtime scheduler). Returns 1 ‚áí GPU. */                
      1427 +static int cg_placement_prefer_gpu(const MachineProfile *p, d
           +ouble flops_per_elem, int ncol, long rows) {                 
      1428 +  if (!p->gpu_present || p->gpu_gflops <= 0 || p->cpu_gflops 
           +<= 0 || rows <= 0)                                           
      1429 +    return 0;                                                
      1430 +  double total_flops = flops_per_elem * (double)rows;        
      1431 +  double bytes = (double)ncol * 4.0 * (double)rows; /* one co
           +lumn set, float */                                           
      1432 +  double up = (p->pcie_up_gbps > 0) ? bytes / (p->pcie_up_gbp
           +s * 1e9) : 1e30;                                             
      1433 +  double down = (p->pcie_down_gbps > 0) ? bytes / (p->pcie_do
           +wn_gbps * 1e9) : 1e30;                                       
      1434 +  double gpu_t = p->gpu_launch_us * 1e-6 + up + down + total_
           +flops / (p->gpu_gflops * 1e9);                               
      1435 +  double cpu_t = total_flops / (p->cpu_gflops * 1e9);        
      1436 +  return gpu_t < cpu_t;                                      
      1437 +}                                                            
      1438 +

      1441    const char *rtail = rdot ? rdot + 1 : name;

‚óŹ Slice 4 is complete and fully green.

  Slice 4 landed: derived CPU/GPU placement via a per-machine calibration phase

  This is the slice your "per-user comptime" insight reshaped ‚ÄĒ and it resolves
  the long-standing tension cleanly.

  The architecture you identified: placement is a runtime decision in
  StarPU/Legion because cost constants are machine-specific. arche resolves it
  with a per-machine calibration phase whose decision is frozen ‚ÄĒ no runtime
  scheduler. Static pools mean row counts are known too, so every cost input
  (calibrated constants + derived intensity + static size) is in hand at build
  time. Because arche compiles from source on the host (like -march=native),
  this folds into arche build: a machine profile is measured once, cached in
  ARCHE_CACHE_DIR, reused.

  What's implemented:
  - Eligibility is free post-Slice-3: a pure map is kind==MAP && !eff
  (branchless + effect-free), so under --gpu every pure map is GPU-eligible with
  no @gpu annotation (@gpu survives as a force-override).
  - Cost model (cg_placement_prefer_gpu) + an arithmetic-intensity walk read the
  profile + static row count to decide GPU vs CPU per map, frozen into the
  schedule.
  - arche calibrate (new subcommand): measures cpu_gflops in-process and probes
  the GPU by building+running a tiny kernel through the normal --gpu pipeline ‚ÄĒ
  keeping the compiler itself Vulkan-free.
  - Showcase bench (derived_placement.arche, zero annotations) + make 
  test-placement proving the derivation: membound‚ÜíCPU, heavy‚ÜíGPU.

  Honest result on this box (GTX 1650 / PCIe): the calibration probe shows the
  GPU is overhead-dominated ‚ÄĒ per-dispatch launch+transfer swamps compute for
  realistic kernels ‚ÄĒ so calibration correctly declines to auto-place on it
  (CPU-only), matching the earlier benchmark. The mechanism is validated
  end-to-end under a balanced synthetic profile. So the deliverable is exactly
  what was promised: correct, calibrated, reproducible decisions + a real
  profile ‚ÄĒ not a fabricated GPU win.

  Docs capture the durable contribution: static-mapper.md now reads "fold the
  mapper into a per-machine arche build calibration phase" with a "Landed (Slice
  4)" section, plus the prior art (FFTW wisdom / ATLAS /
  StarPU-perfmodels-but-frozen / TVM).

  Verification ‚ÄĒ all green: lit 897/897, corpus, test-gpu-exe (3),
  test-placement, verify-fmt (935), all six C unit suites. test-doc unchanged.

  Slices 3+4 are uncommitted (1+2 you'd committed). The clean follow-on is Slice
  5 ‚ÄĒ residency-class derivation (a read-walk sibling of the write-walk ‚Üí
  replace @resident/gpu.sync), then distribution (--portable).

  Same source, no annotations ‚Üí different correct placement per machine, decided
  from the cached profile. A static @gpu is baked into the source and cannot be
  right on both machines at once.

  Verdict

  - Correctness: yes ‚ÄĒ the derivation matches measured ground-truth optimal here
  (4/4), where the explicit flag is 0/4.
  - Why it beats the flag: @gpu is a machine-blind, compile-time-fixed
  assertion; the derived decision is calibrated to the actual machine and
  adapts. The flag's failure mode is exactly what your "cost constants are
  per-machine" insight predicted.
  - Two honest caveats: (1) these are non-resident numbers ‚ÄĒ @resident (Slice 5,
  not built) would cut the GPU's transfer cost, though the earlier physics
  benchmark showed GPU still lost even resident; the mapper would re-derive once
  residency facts feed it. (2) The "balanced machine" column is a synthetic
  profile, not measured hardware ‚ÄĒ it shows the mechanism flips correctly; a
  machine where the GPU actually wins would make those GPU calls measured wins
  too.

  GPU compute here runs ~6√ó faster per flop than the CPU; once residency +
  enough dispatches hide the transfer, that throughput advantage wins. The
  earlier losses weren't "GPU is useless" ‚ÄĒ they were transfer-bound and
  overhead-bound single-pass kernels, which is exactly where the CPU should win.

  The honest connection to what I built: Slice 4's cost model is per-dispatch 
  and assumes non-resident transfer every time (GPU_t = launch + transfer + 
  compute). So it correctly keeps single-pass maps on the CPU ‚ÄĒ but it would not
  yet pick GPU for the case above, because it doesn't model "transfer once,
  then loop." Capturing this win is precisely Slice 5 (residency derivation):
  feed an amortized transfer term (one upload + N reuses, derived from the
  schedule's repeated dispatch on a written-once/read-many column) into the same
  cost model, and these resident-loop kernels flip to GPU ‚ÄĒ matching the 2.9√ó I
  just measured.

  So the full picture is consistent and honest:
  - Single-pass / small / non-resident ‚Üí CPU wins ‚Üí derived placement (Slice¬†4)
  picks CPU ‚úď (4/4 earlier).
  - Resident + iterated + large ‚Üí GPU wins (measured 2.9√ó) ‚Üí needs the
  residency/schedule terms (Slice¬†5) for the mapper to see it.

  Want me to make Slice 5 fold residency + repeated-dispatch into the cost model
  so the mapper derives this GPU win (no @resident, no @gpu) ‚ÄĒ and add this
  resident-loop case as the bench arm that shows the mapper choosing GPU and
  being right?

  So, precisely:

  Where it derives correctly: single-pass / non-resident kernels ‚ÄĒ it matched
  measured-optimal 4/4 earlier (all CPU, where the GPU genuinely loses).

  Where it does not (the resident-loop win): on this box it derives CPU ‚ÄĒ wrong
  ‚ÄĒ for two compounding reasons:
  1. Calibration false-negative. My arche calibrate set gpu_present=0 because
  its probe was a single-pass kernel where the GPU is overhead-bound ‚ÄĒ so the
  mapper never even considers the GPU here, even though the GPU wins 2.9√ó in the
  resident-loop regime. The calibration threw away a real win.
  2. The cost model is per-dispatch + non-resident. It computes launch + 
  transfer + compute for one dispatch and assumes the transfer happens every
  time. It has no term for "upload once, reuse across 40 dispatches." Under the
  balanced profile it happened to say GPU ‚ÄĒ but only because fpe=64 at 16M rows
  beats even a per-dispatch transfer in that arithmetic; it's not modeling the
  amortization that actually makes the win, so it'd be right by luck and wrong
  in nearby cases (fewer flops, more dispatches).

  So the verdict is honest and unflattering for that case: the mapper is correct
  only inside the regime it models. It does not yet derive the resident-loop
  GPU win ‚ÄĒ that's the precise boundary of Slice 4.

  What makes it derive correctly there ‚ÄĒ Slice 5:
  - Calibration records the separate GPU constants (launch, bandwidth, gflops)
  instead of a blanket "not worth it," so the cost model can apply them
  per-kernel-per-size.
  - The cost model gains a residency + amortization term: from the schedule it
  sees a column written-once/read-many across K dispatches and a
  @resident-eligible pool, so transfer cost is one upload / K not √ó K. Then
  heavy @resident, K=40 derives GPU, and it derives it because of the real
  amortization ‚ÄĒ matching the 2.9√ó measurement.

  If you want, Slice 5 is exactly this: residency-class derivation + an
  amortized-transfer cost term + a calibration that keeps the GPU constants ‚ÄĒ
  turning that false-negative into a derived, correct GPU placement with no
  annotations. Want me to plan it?

‚óŹ I could only extract the search results, not the paper/slides PDFs (they're
  image-encoded), so I'll be explicit about what's verified vs inferred.

  What AutoMap actually does (verified from the abstract/summary)

  AutoMap (Teixeira, Henzinger, Yadav, Aiken ‚ÄĒ SC'23) is a constrained 
  coordinate-wise descent search over the mapping space (a processor per task +
  a memory per region collection). It automatically tunes the mapping to the 
  hardware used, with no user code, and finds mappings up to 2.41√ó faster than 
  hand-written mappers. The objective explicitly trades off compute speed vs. 
  data movement.

  The load-bearing word is search: it explores candidate mappings and optimizes
  an objective, adapting to the actual machine. (Inferred, since I couldn't
  extract the body: a coordinate-descent that "tunes to the hardware used"
  almost certainly evaluates candidates by running/profiling, the way Legion's
  profiler supports ‚ÄĒ not by a hand-written closed-form. I'd want to confirm
  against the paper text before treating that as fact.)

  Is that what we were doing? No ‚ÄĒ we did roughly the opposite

  ‚Ēā adaptivity  ‚Ēā searches per            ‚Ēā one blanket verdict from one    ‚Ēā
  ‚Ēā             ‚Ēā program/hardware        ‚Ēā probe kernel                    ‚Ēā
  ‚ĒĒ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēī‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēī‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēė

  So our cg_placement_prefer_gpu is a hand-rolled cost model ‚ÄĒ the thing AutoMap
  replaces, not the thing AutoMap is. Our static-mapper.md even soft-pedaled
  this ("the placement policy can be inferred") ‚ÄĒ that was imprecise; AutoMap
  doesn't infer a policy, it searches.

  Why our decisions were wrong, through that lens

  The resident-loop false negative (derived CPU; measured GPU 2.8√ó faster) is a
  textbook model-vs-measurement failure. Our closed form was blind to three
  things a measurement would have caught for free:

  1. Effective throughput. The model assumed peak gpu_gflops. The real kernel
  ran at ~37 Gflops effective (‚Čą50√ó below peak ‚ÄĒ inefficient dispatch). No
  closed form knew that; running it would have.
  2. Residency. The model bakes in a transfer every dispatch; it has no "upload
  once, reuse" term.
  3. Schedule structure. It scores one dispatch; it can't see the K=40 loop that
  makes the amortization pay off.

  And the calibration compounded it: one probe ‚Üí gpu_present=0 ‚Üí applied to all
  kernels. We collapsed the whole per-kernel/per-size/per-residency decision
  into 5 numbers + a formula ‚ÄĒ discarding exactly the structure that determines
  the answer.

  The real conclusion

  The AutoMap-consistent fix is measure, don't model ‚ÄĒ and arche is positioned
  to do it better than AutoMap. AutoMap must search at runtime because Legion's
  sizes/graph are dynamic. arche has static pools + a folded schedule + the 
  kernel source, so at build time it can literally compile each eligible map
  both ways, run it at its real (static) size, and freeze the measured winner ‚ÄĒ
  empirical autotuning (FFTW/ATLAS/AutoMap-style) with zero runtime cost. That
  gets the resident-loop case right by construction. The analytical model should
  be at most a cheap pre-filter; the decision should be empirical.

  So: the wrong calls weren't a tuning bug ‚ÄĒ they're the predictable cost of
  choosing a coarse analytical model over measurement, which is the one choice
  AutoMap exists to argue against.

  Want me to (a) verify the measurement-in-the-loop claim against the paper text
  another way, or (b) sketch the "build-time measure-both-ways, freeze winner"
  redesign as the real Slice 5?

  Sources:
  - AutoMap paper (SC'23)
  - Legion publications
  - AutoMap artifact (Zenodo)

‚ĚĮ explain a vs b                                                                

‚óŹ (a) ‚ÄĒ confirm what AutoMap actually does. I claimed its search likely
  evaluates mappings by measuring real runs, but I flagged that as inference
  because the PDFs wouldn't extract. (a) is a small read-only research step: get
  the method confirmed from a source I can actually read ‚ÄĒ the Zenodo
  artifact's code/README, the Legion abstract page, or an HTML/cached version of
  the paper. Outcome: either "yes, AutoMap measures in the loop" (so my
  "measure, don't model" conclusion is grounded in the prior art) or "actually
  it uses a learned/analytical model" (which would change the lesson). It
  changes no code ‚ÄĒ it just makes sure the argument rests on facts, not my
  memory. Cheap; ~one or two fetches.

  (b) ‚ÄĒ build the fix. This is the actual redesign that corrects the wrong
  decisions. Today we predict placement from a closed-form model (launch + 
  bytes/pcie + flops/gflops), and it mispredicted the resident-loop case. (b)
  replaces the predictor with build-time measurement: for each GPU-eligible map,
  the build compiles it both ways, runs it at its real static size (or a scaled
  proxy), times CPU vs GPU, and freezes the measured winner into the schedule.
  Because arche has static pool sizes + the kernel source + a folded schedule,
  all of this is knowable at build time ‚ÄĒ so it's empirical autotuning with zero
  runtime cost, and it gets the resident-loop GPU win right by construction
  (it'd measure 2.8√ó and pick GPU). It's the real Slice 5, and it's substantial:
  a build-time micro-runner, handling residency/loop structure in the measured
  workload, caching results per (kernel, machine). Bigger, changes real code.

  They're complementary, not exclusive: (a) justifies (b) ‚ÄĒ if AutoMap confirms
  measurement beats modeling, that's the citation backing the redesign. Natural
  order is (a) then (b). But if you already buy "measure beats model" here, we
  can skip straight to (b).
